<div id="review_539932647" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/539932647" />
    <a title="Dem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2752994-dem"><img alt="Dem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552868566p2/2752994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/539932647?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer539932647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14527281975878189289"><b> 3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Calling Me Home by Julie Kibler is a beautiful debut Novel telling the story of a forbidden love in 1930s Kentucky with a modern-day friendship.<br/><br/>Eighty nine year old Isabelle McAllister has a favour to ask her hairdresser Dorrie Curtis. It's a big one. Isabelle wants Dorrie, a black single mom in her thirties, to drop everything to drive her from her home in Arlington, Texas, to a funeral in Cincinnati. With no clear explanation why and they must leave the following day. Dorrie is plagu</span>
  <span id="freeText14527281975878189289" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Calling Me Home by Julie Kibler is a beautiful debut Novel telling the story of a forbidden love in 1930s Kentucky with a modern-day friendship.<br /><br />Eighty nine year old Isabelle McAllister has a favour to ask her hairdresser Dorrie Curtis. It's a big one. Isabelle wants Dorrie, a black single mom in her thirties, to drop everything to drive her from her home in Arlington, Texas, to a funeral in Cincinnati. With no clear explanation why and they must leave the following day. Dorrie is plagued with problems of her own but not wanting to let her friend down she agrees to drive Isabelle to the Funeral.<br /><br />There is so much to love about this book and to be honest once again I was drawn in by the cover and the blurb of this Novel<br />This is one of those books that you pick up and you seem to settle into the story within a few chapters. Julie Kibler has painted two wonderful characters that are very well thought out and by the end of the story you feel you know these two women. I especially loved and envied the friendship between Miss Isabelle and Dorrie as easy friendships like these are hard to come by. I loved how these two strong woman came together and gave each other support and without any pressure or any expectations of each other. <br /><br />Julie Kibler also tackles the difficult issue of racial equality and I believe that this novel was inspired by a relationship her grandmother had. <br />Calling Me Home is a book that is going to appeal to so many people and this is certainly more than a story about racial equality, it is a story about hope love and friendships that come along once in a lifetime.<br /><br />This is a well written historical fiction novel and I certainly will be recommending this book to many of my friends as it had wonderful reader appeal.<br /><br />Definitely worth cosying up on the couch for this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14527281975878189289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2905227914" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Debbie Oliphant" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46372377-debbie-oliphant"><img alt="Debbie Oliphant" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2905227914?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie Oliphant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie Oliphant" href="/user/show/46372377-debbie-oliphant">Debbie Oliphant</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2905227914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14586449469389614429">Oh boy, where do I begin. I am emotionally drained after finishing this amazing book and would love to add 5 more stars to the rating.<br/><br/>I was drawn in from the first chapter with Miss Isabelle's urgent request to Dorrie, her hairdresser and friend, to take her to a funeral. She doesn't reveal anything else, yet Dorrie knows this is important and she complies. The thousand mile road trip unweaves a secret that Miss Isabelle has not had the courage to share and was too painful to tell. But little by</span>
  <span id="freeText14586449469389614429" style="display:none">Oh boy, where do I begin. I am emotionally drained after finishing this amazing book and would love to add 5 more stars to the rating.<br /><br />I was drawn in from the first chapter with Miss Isabelle's urgent request to Dorrie, her hairdresser and friend, to take her to a funeral. She doesn't reveal anything else, yet Dorrie knows this is important and she complies. The thousand mile road trip unweaves a secret that Miss Isabelle has not had the courage to share and was too painful to tell. But little by little, she reveals to Dorrie the events that have shaped her to the 89 year old woman she is today. Dorrie is such a thoughtful, wonderful friend who understands the heartache Miss Isabelle endured and sees parallels in her own life. <br /><br />This story is a reminder that love is love and while the thought was forbidden during the time, the main characters found a way to test that affirmation even for a little while. Be prepared for the many feels and bring lots of tissues.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14586449469389614429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2777032445" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2777032445" />
    <a title="Amber’s reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36408777-amber-s-reading"><img alt="Amber’s reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507753197p2/36408777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2777032445?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber’s reading" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber’s reading" href="/user/show/36408777-amber-s-reading">Amber’s reading</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2777032445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15638350052328937908">Calling Me Home reads like a movie. I could envision every little detail. Some of it was beautiful and some so deplorable that my heart ached. <br/><br/>The story is told in my absolute favorite way - starting at the end with hints and then going back to the beginning. It’s the story of a middle aged African American mother and hairdresser being asked by her 89-year-old white client to take her on a road trip to attend a funeral. <br/><br/>While on this road trip, the older woman tells her story about how she fell </span>
  <span id="freeText15638350052328937908" style="display:none">Calling Me Home reads like a movie. I could envision every little detail. Some of it was beautiful and some so deplorable that my heart ached. <br /><br />The story is told in my absolute favorite way - starting at the end with hints and then going back to the beginning. It’s the story of a middle aged African American mother and hairdresser being asked by her 89-year-old white client to take her on a road trip to attend a funeral. <br /><br />While on this road trip, the older woman tells her story about how she fell in love with a young black man when she was a teenager, but they were forbidden to be together. She talks about her life, her family, the racism in her small town, and how hatred and fear prevented so many things. But all the while, not telling who’s funeral they are attending. <br /><br />I loved this book. It was heartbreaking but tender and I wanted so badly for things to turn out differently. The way the story unfolded was very unique and even though I saw certain things coming, the author did have some surprises up her sleeve. <br /><br />Even though things have changed, we have so much further to go. Love and acceptance conquers all. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15638350052328937908" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/469798959" />
    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/469798959?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer469798959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12997373339000306051">3.5 This was a heartfelt, poignant story about a love across the color divide in the 1930's, when this was not something that was accepted. Really loved the relationships in this novel, Isie being so much older but a good friend to Dorrie all the same. Together they brought closure and a new way of looking at the problems they needed to solve. These are the two characters with a few more that I will remember from this story. Racial affairs, relationships, and friendship were all explored in this</span>
  <span id="freeText12997373339000306051" style="display:none">3.5 This was a heartfelt, poignant story about a love across the color divide in the 1930's, when this was not something that was accepted. Really loved the relationships in this novel, Isie being so much older but a good friend to Dorrie all the same. Together they brought closure and a new way of looking at the problems they needed to solve. These are the two characters with a few more that I will remember from this story. Racial affairs, relationships, and friendship were all explored in this story. This was a wonderful novel to curl up with, watching the snow coming down, creating a beautiful landscape, in which to read a bout a love that was beautiful but could never be. A sentimental story for sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12997373339000306051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Sofia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14453898-sofia"><img alt="Sofia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404331721p2/14453898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1165970396?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia" href="/user/show/14453898-sofia">Sofia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14453898-sofia?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165970396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12377922264883551386">I never purposely choose books that make be cry. Crying is not a kink of mine. This one snuck up on me with stealth via my friend Ingela. Oh I knew from the blurb that there was a possibility but I decided to join in the read anyway.<br/><br/>Did I cry? – OH YES LOTS. Am I angry? – OH YES at the bigotry, racism dealt with in the story. Angrier, more and more, that we still have to deal with this even in our day and age both within us and in the world we live in. I liked that Kibler did not shy away from e</span>
  <span id="freeText12377922264883551386" style="display:none">I never purposely choose books that make be cry. Crying is not a kink of mine. This one snuck up on me with stealth via my friend Ingela. Oh I knew from the blurb that there was a possibility but I decided to join in the read anyway.<br><br>Did I cry? – OH YES LOTS. Am I angry? – OH YES at the bigotry, racism dealt with in the story. Angrier, more and more, that we still have to deal with this even in our day and age both within us and in the world we live in. I liked that Kibler did not shy away from exploring a bit the racist that lives within each and every one of us. We have to acknowledge this before starting to move forward. It is a battle I think that each of us has to fight, each in the context of our lives.<br><br>While I like both stories Isa’s and Dorrie’s, I think I preferred the first three quarters of the book when the tears were still at bay. After that the emotional tugging went into overdrive and I get the feeling that yes it drained me emotionally but my brain was left dry. I had difficulty yes accepting Isa and Robert’s wide eyed naivety at what they were entering into. Is it realistic, possibly, not all of us view the world pragmatically especially during our teenage, rose coloured years, the time when we think that just by trying we are able to change the world. And like us Isa and Robert paid dearly for that naivety.<br><br>Dorrie’s story might not have been as high profile as Isa but I liked her and the story she told, of the doubts that beset us all the time and the decisions we take and how and where we find inspiration.<br><br><pre> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421867344i/13423631.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></pre><br><br>BR with Ingela and Irina who drag me along where I wouldn't normally go :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="12377922264883551386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The relationship between Dorrie and Isabelle was special because they simply liked each other for who they were, without concern for skin color or age.. What a bond between these two women!<br/><br/>I loved the way the author unfolded the story of Isabelle’s past in between chapters of Dorrie’s current life challenges. My heart ached for Isabelle’s lost love. I rooted for Dorrie to find peace with her struggles and worries. And </span>
  <span id="freeText16618742465267880968" style="display:none">My Thoughts<br /><br />Not many stories make me cry, but the ending of this one sure did. The relationship between Dorrie and Isabelle was special because they simply liked each other for who they were, without concern for skin color or age.. What a bond between these two women!<br /><br />I loved the way the author unfolded the story of Isabelle’s past in between chapters of Dorrie’s current life challenges. My heart ached for Isabelle’s lost love. I rooted for Dorrie to find peace with her struggles and worries. And the ending - OY!<br /><br />This is a debut novel for Ms. Kibler. What beautiful, beautiful writing.<br /><br />I am thrilled to have been given the opportunity to read this in exchange for an unbiased review. Many thanks to St. Martin’s Press and Netgalley.<br /><br />Publish date: February 12, 2013.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/506596463" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/506596463?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/722391-pamela">Pamela</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer506596463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7148817912605971153">You might read reviews of Julie Kibler's debut novel that compare it to The Help or even To Kill a Mockingbird. And while Kibler's story certainly contains a healthy dose of racism and conflict, the heart of the book is a love story--a tragic tale of forbidden love and the consequences that love carries with it throughout generations. While it seems redundant to summarize the book here, I will say that Isabelle's story is one that grasps you from the first chapter and won't let you go. <br/><br/>Kibler we</span>
  <span id="freeText7148817912605971153" style="display:none">You might read reviews of Julie Kibler's debut novel that compare it to The Help or even To Kill a Mockingbird. And while Kibler's story certainly contains a healthy dose of racism and conflict, the heart of the book is a love story--a tragic tale of forbidden love and the consequences that love carries with it throughout generations. While it seems redundant to summarize the book here, I will say that Isabelle's story is one that grasps you from the first chapter and won't let you go. <br /><br />Kibler weaves a tale that binds two women from different backgrounds, different generations and defines 'family' without regard to skin color or economics. It causes us to examine the people in our lives who cross our paths and change us for the better. You won't want to miss this novel. You most certainly won't want it to end! </span>

<div id="review_1520981125" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1520981125" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29279709-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458171712p2/29279709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1520981125?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/29279709-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1520981125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer103455036320292036">Calling Me Home by Julie Kibler<br/>I loved this book, it was such a great story. When I had to put it down I could not wait to get back to it. You know, when you are reading something that you wish the book would not end. when you have only a quarter of the book left. The time period shifts back and forth from the 1930's to the present day. Isabelle who is white asks her African american hair stylist named Dorrie to drive her to a funereal from Kentucky to Ohio.<br/><br/>Isabelle is in her nineties and Dorrie</span>
  <span id="freeText103455036320292036" style="display:none">Calling Me Home by Julie Kibler<br />I loved this book, it was such a great story. When I had to put it down I could not wait to get back to it. You know, when you are reading something that you wish the book would not end. when you have only a quarter of the book left. The time period shifts back and forth from the 1930's to the present day. Isabelle who is white asks her African american hair stylist named Dorrie to drive her to a funereal from Kentucky to Ohio.<br /><br />Isabelle is in her nineties and Dorrie has two teenagers who she is raising alone. Dorrie is fed up with meeting men who for her have been bad luck and Isabelle has an interesting story to tell.<br />This book is about friendships. Its about finding your soulmate. It is about racism in the deep South.<br /><br />Isabelle grows up with a racist mother and two older brothers. Isabelle and her father are not racist. Isabelle tells Dorrie about her life growing up in a southern town where African american's cannot be in town after dark. There is a big sign going in and out of town that states that no African americans can be in the town or on the streets after dark/. This fictional town in Kentucky borders a state where it is okay with the law for White people to marry African americans.<br /><br />Cora and Nell and Robert all work for Isabelle's family by day, but at night they have to be home before sunset. Isabelle and Robert get romantically involved secretly. What happens between Isabelle and Robert? How would you feel if your soul mate was a different ethnic background from you and your own family not to mention the state had laws against you getting married? Would you follow your heart? This is an aged old dilemma that is spun into a story that will captivate you and break your heart. I am truly sorry that I finished reading this story. The pages turn themselves and there is a twist of an ending that totally surprised me.. <br /><br />It is an old story that is told in a refreshing, imaginative new way. It is a redeeming story. One that I will recommend highly. I will not forget this book. Five Stars </span>
  <a data-text-id="103455036320292036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1257800137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257800137" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20048096-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598408667p2/20048096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257800137?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/20048096-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Pamela by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/31780425-linda-johnson">Linda Johnson</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=love">love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=race-relations">race-relations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=southern-fiction">southern-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=texas">texas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=grief">grief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=kentucky">kentucky</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257800137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11103517070041042980">"It's an irony that young people mostly see things as black and white . . . All or nothing. Sometimes, in spite of their enthusiasm for embracing change, it takes years of experience before they truly see the whole picture." <br/><br/>And sometimes it takes a lifetime to find the right person (a kindred spirit, a true and rare friend) in which to share the secrets never before spoken. <br/><br/>Two women. One relatively young, the other considerably aged. One with ebony hair and skin, the other whitish-blue. Both s</span>
  <span id="freeText11103517070041042980" style="display:none">"It's an irony that young people mostly see things as black and white . . . All or nothing. Sometimes, in spite of their enthusiasm for embracing change, it takes years of experience before they truly see the whole picture." <br /><br />And sometimes it takes a lifetime to find the right person (a kindred spirit, a true and rare friend) in which to share the secrets never before spoken. <br /><br />Two women. One relatively young, the other considerably aged. One with ebony hair and skin, the other whitish-blue. Both seeking answers to voids in their past and present lives. And on a road trip from Arlington to Cincinnati, as stories are told and secrets immerge, they both might find their worlds turned upside-right in surprising ways. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15793184.Calling_Me_Home" title="Calling Me Home by Julie Kibler" rel="nofollow noopener">Calling Me Home</a> is a story of joys and sorrows, secrets and revelations, love and loss, courage and fear, friendship and family, prejudice and acceptance, crossroads and dead-ends. It's also a journey. A literary portal connecting and comparing the past with the present through themes that bring to light (subtly and not so subtly) issues surrounding coming-of-age, parenthood, first loves, social customs, family dysfunctions, race/gender/age stereotyping, and the bigoted cruelty of racism. <br /><br />"These little sundown towns had been established everywhere - north or south of the Mason Dixon line, east or wet of the Great Divide. Maybe it wasn't as in your face now as it had been back then, maybe it was no longer politically correct to keep someone out of your town just because of skin color, but that didn't stop some folks."<br /><br />Oh, but not everything is dour or heartbreaking or ultra-serious. Along the way there are moments of hilarity, mystery, intrigue, and witty wisdom.<br /><br />"Anyone who thinks a seventeen-year old is mature enough to always know the difference between a smart choice and a dumbass decision hasn't been a mother to a seventeen-year-old."<br /><br />Told through altering voices and eras - Dorrie and Isabelle/present and flashback - rich with atmosphere, emotion, and intrigue, makes for a compelling and endearing story. Something about the way in which it's woven together (not the story itself) reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9375.Fried_Green_Tomatoes_at_the_Whistle_Stop_Cafe" title="Fried Green Tomatoes at the Whistle Stop Cafe by Fannie Flagg" rel="nofollow noopener">Fried Green Tomatoes at the Whistle Stop Cafe</a>. Which, in my opinion, is a wonderful thing. And it rings authentic, both in story and dialogue. I also think it's quite amazing for a debut novel. Certainly it's no wonder the ratings on Goodreads are so high; it's a novel that deserves accolades. <br /><br />Overall, except for the too-neatly-tied-in-a-convenient-melodrama-bow-resolve, a really great read. <br /><br />Four exceptionally strong stars. <br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11103517070041042980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3029752263" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3029752263" />
    <a title="Lynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15265939-lynn"><img alt="Lynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356920956p2/15265939.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3029752263?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynn" href="/user/show/15265939-lynn">Lynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250020437" href="/book/show/17934422-calling-me-home">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15265939-lynn?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15265939-lynn?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3029752263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13841033511598697612">4.5 stars rounded up. <br/><br/>This book was a slow start for me, but once I got into the story and the rhythm of the narrative, I couldn’t put it down. <br/><br/>89 year old Isabelle asks a big favor of her hairdresser Dorrie: please drive her from Arlington, TX to Cincinnati, OH to attend a funeral. Tomorrow. Dorrie is a black, single mother with worries of her own, but she drops everything to bring Isabelle to this funeral, without knowing any of the details. While on the road together, Isabelle tells Dorrie th</span>
  <span id="freeText13841033511598697612" style="display:none">4.5 stars rounded up. <br /><br />This book was a slow start for me, but once I got into the story and the rhythm of the narrative, I couldn’t put it down. <br /><br />89 year old Isabelle asks a big favor of her hairdresser Dorrie: please drive her from Arlington, TX to Cincinnati, OH to attend a funeral. Tomorrow. Dorrie is a black, single mother with worries of her own, but she drops everything to bring Isabelle to this funeral, without knowing any of the details. While on the road together, Isabelle tells Dorrie the story of her life, including her ill fated relationship with the son of her family’s black housekeeper. Dorrie also reveals the problems in her own life, and the two women form an even stronger bond during their road trip. <br /><br />Isabelle and Dorrie are extraordinary characters. You learn so much about them as the book alternates between Isabelle’s life in the 1930s and 40s, when she was a 17 year old girl growing up in a racially divided Kentucky town, experiencing her first love with a forbidden boy; and the present day as Dorrie copes with her son’s problems and her own shaky history with men. <br /><br />Throughout the book, the big mystery is whose funeral are they going to. I admit that I figured it out about halfway through the book, as Isabelle reveals more and more about her past. The ending of the book just about broke my heart, as well as filled my heart with love. I could absolutely identify with Isabelle’s dilemma: loving a boy she was forbidden to have. In college, I was forced to give up my boyfriend because of religious differences. Ironically, I later married a man of a different religion, but by then my family had no say in the matter, since I was a self supporting adult. And at age 39, my mother was just relieved that I got married at all. <br /><br />The book is beautifully written and the segues between time periods is almost seamless. There are so many issues explored in this book: civil rights; racial discrimination; abortion; family relationships; heartbreak; interpersonal relationships between races and generations; lost love and learning to love and trust again. The story is told with great sensitivity and touches of humor. <br /><br />This book is a definite recommend and I look forward to reading more books by Julie Kibler. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13841033511598697612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_828366299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/828366299" />
    <a title="Judy D Collins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11063006-judy-d-collins"><img alt="Judy D Collins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577847504p2/11063006.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/828366299?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judy D Collins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judy D Collins" href="/user/show/11063006-judy-d-collins">Judy D Collins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11063006-judy-d-collins?shelf=debut-novel">debut-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11063006-judy-d-collins?shelf=books-read-in-2014">books-read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11063006-judy-d-collins?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11063006-judy-d-collins?shelf=racial">racial</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11063006-judy-d-collins?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11063006-judy-d-collins?shelf=southern-fiction">southern-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11063006-judy-d-collins?shelf=julie-kibler">julie-kibler</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer828366299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16089028492111515763">Julie Kibler's <b>CALLING ME HOME</b>, a poignant, debut novel; a winner out of the gate, filled with careful description and woven skillfully! <br/><br/><b>A vivid, engaging first book</b> with strong characters, dramatic storytelling, which should establish <i>Julie Kibler </i> as a strong novelist. She most definitely possesses a gift of telling a tragic story, in an entertaining way with an inspiring takeaway of friendship and love. <i>(She has just been added to my favorite author list, and so look forward to following this</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16089028492111515763" style="display:none">Julie Kibler's <b>CALLING ME HOME</b>, a poignant, debut novel; a winner out of the gate, filled with careful description and woven skillfully! <br /><br /><b>A vivid, engaging first book</b> with strong characters, dramatic storytelling, which should establish <i>Julie Kibler </i> as a strong novelist. She most definitely possesses a gift of telling a tragic story, in an entertaining way with an inspiring takeaway of friendship and love. <i>(She has just been added to my favorite author list, and so look forward to following this author)!</i><br /><br /><b>A complex and compelling portrait</b> of the painful intricacies of love, loyalty, discrimination, and racial tensions. An insightful story of two women caught between their hearts, families, and their future. <br /> <br /><b>CALLING ME HOME </b> no ordinary love story; however, a book of astonishing precision from past to present, from one younger black woman and an older white woman; raw, painful, beautiful feelings told in honesty, unfolding precisely and eloquently, during this long road trip between friends of two different eras and color. <br /><br /><b>The real magic </b> of the book was the subject matter of two families (black/white) trying to survive in an era in which men and women found themselves bound by strict constraints, dictated by society and ignorance. A heartfelt story and forbidden love of two people –fighting for a life they so deserve – a fearless, heart-wrenching story about the power of true love and friendship. <br /><br /><b>There was much depth and power </b> to this relationship between Robert/Isabelle; a timeless love derailed by others, secrets, and an era which did not accept this sort of relationship between a man and woman. A complex tapestry of lives intertwined a compassionate story of those who are destroyed by love by secrets and betrayal. <br /><br />Warmth and love, even with such painful subjects, as the bond these two women share, not bound by blood, but by a friendship which changes Dottie’s life and her future, is remarkable – a portrait of resilience told with clarity and painful precision, probing the dark history of Isabelle’s past with a few surprises readers will love before it ends, making you smile.<br /><br /><b>An emotionally charged, </b> absorbing novel about friends, lovers, secrets, and families. Kibler’s sensitive and gripping examination of a family’s past is engaging from the beginning and gets better with every chapter, with unforgettable characters. Eloquently told and making it more special, the author’s insight into the subject matter from her family’s history. <br /><br />A powerful and memorable story you will not soon forget. Ideal for book clubs and discussions. Cannot wait for her next book. For fans of Catherine Ryan Hyde, Laura Lane McNeal, and Bette Lee Crosby. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.judithdcollinsconsulting.com/#!Calling-Me-Home/cmoa/20B20E62-8DFE-49F8-970B-683376744233" rel="nofollow noopener">JDCMustReadBooks </a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.judithdcollinsconsulting.com/#!top-books-of-2014/c1860" rel="nofollow noopener"> TOP 30 BOOKS OF 2014 </a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16089028492111515763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3637848551757433498">I loved this book! Julie Kibler is an amazing first time novelist! I hope she is busy writing her next book, because I can't wait to read it! I hesitated to spend $12 on a kindle book, but it was so worth it! I have to say the first third of the book was a little slow, but midway through, I couldn't put it down. I felt attached to Dorrie, & especially Isabelle. I was drawn to this book, after being in an interracial relationship myself, years ago. I had a taste of how hurtful people can be towar</span>
  <span id="freeText3637848551757433498" style="display:none">I loved this book! Julie Kibler is an amazing first time novelist! I hope she is busy writing her next book, because I can't wait to read it! I hesitated to spend $12 on a kindle book, but it was so worth it! I have to say the first third of the book was a little slow, but midway through, I couldn't put it down. I felt attached to Dorrie, &amp; especially Isabelle. I was drawn to this book, after being in an interracial relationship myself, years ago. I had a taste of how hurtful people can be towards couples of different races. This special story brought tears to my eyes more than once. the relationship between the two ladies as they traveled together was heartwarming. It reminded me of a couple of elderly lady friends I have grown to love. I will recommend it to my friends.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9BLzp6ZbzsfQ3PiRUE206d4r/14xQfZKBTVBt0X2Ld5CSs8jZ/oNL6wyURvwq+NblkirCtm5ozFYoeFSocn+xg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+JR/79aWmQvgor9WsFL0XZddW8gxN7eRqdMeCZsYWtBOzENrFzda45xMFtwQtKPv3z4PnNnP4ur0R77sfyeJyA==')})
  }

And though they face all kinds of dangers in a landscape that is at times breathtakingly beautiful, at others brutal, they’re committed to their job: bringing books to people who have never had any, arming them with facts that will change their lives.\n\nBased on a true story rooted in America’s past, The Giver of Stars is unparalleled in its scope and epic in its storytelling. <span id="freeTextContainer11617094225430622516">Julie Kibler is the bestselling author of Home for Erring and Outcast Girls and Calling Me Home, which was an IndieNext List pick, Target Club Pick, and Ladies' Home Journal Book Club Pick, published in fifteen languages. She has a bachelor's degree in English and journalism and a master's degree in library science and lives with her family, including four rescued dogs and cats, in Texas.</span>
